mw-body-content">\n</div>\n<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">State religion</h1>\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_state_religions.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Map_of_state_religions.svg/350px-Map_of_state_religions.svg.png" width="350" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Map_of_state_religions.svg/525px-Map_of_state_religions.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Map_of_state_religions.svg/700px-Map_of_state_religions.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_state_religions.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Countries with a state religion. <table>  <tbody><tr valign="top"> <td> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0000FF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a></div> </td> <td><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span> </td> <td> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #158706; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a></div> </td> <td><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span> </td> <td> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #EBCF16; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a></div> </td></tr></tbody></table></div></div></div>\n<p>A <b>state religion</b> (also called an <b>established religion</b> or <b>official religion</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">religious</a> body or <a href="/wiki/Creed" title="Creed">creed</a> officially endorsed by the <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">state</a>. A state with an official religion, while not <a href="/wiki/Secular_state" title="Secular state">secular</a>, is not necessarily a <a href="/wiki/Theocracy" title="Theocracy">theocracy</a>, a country whose rulers have both secular and spiritual authority. State religions are official or government-sanctioned establishments of a religion, but the state does not need be under the control of the religion (as in a theocracy) nor is the state-sanctioned religion necessarily under the control of the state.\n</p><p>Official religions have been known throughout <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_world" title="History of the world">human history</a> in almost all types of cultures, reaching into the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Near_East" title="Ancient Near East">Ancient Near East</a> and prehistory. The relation of <a href="/wiki/Religious_cult" class="mw-redirect" title="Religious cult">religious cult</a> and the state was discussed by <a href="/wiki/Varro" class="mw-redirect" title="Varro">Varro</a>, under the term of <i><a href="/wiki/Theologia_civilis" class="mw-redirect" title="Theologia civilis">theologia civilis</a></i> ("civic theology"). The first state-sponsored <a href="/wiki/Christian_church" class="mw-redirect" title="Christian church">Christian church</a> was the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Apostolic_Church" title="Armenian Apostolic Church">Armenian Apostolic Church</a>, established in 301 CE.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>, as the term <i>church</i> is typically applied to a Christian place of worship or organisations incorporating such ones, the term <i>state church</i> is associated with Christianity as sanctioned by the government, historically the <a href="/wiki/State_church_of_the_Roman_Empire" title="State church of the Roman Empire">state church of the Roman Empire</a> in the last centuries of the Empire\'s existence, and is sometimes used to denote a specific modern national branch of Christianity. Closely related to state churches are <a href="/wiki/Ecclesia_(sociology_of_religion)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecclesia (sociology of religion)">ecclesiae</a>, which are similar but carry a more minor connotation.\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>, many states with primarily Islamic population have <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> as their state religion, either as the <a href="/wiki/Shiite" class="mw-redirect" title="Shiite">Shiite</a> or <a href="/wiki/Sunni" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni">Sunni</a> variety, though the degree of religious restrictions on the citizen\'s everyday life varies by country. <a href="/wiki/Kings_of_Saudi_Arabia" class="mw-redirect" title="Kings of Saudi Arabia">Rulers</a> of Saudi Arabia use both secular and religious power, while Iran\'s secular <a href="/wiki/President_of_Iran" title="President of Iran">presidents</a> are supposed to follow the decisions of <a href="/wiki/Supreme_leader_of_Iran" class="mw-redirect" title="Supreme leader of Iran">religious authorities</a> since the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Revolution" title="Iranian Revolution">revolution of 1979</a>. Turkey, which also has a primarily Muslim population, became a secular country after <a href="/wiki/Atat%C3%BCrk%27s_Reforms" title="Atat\xc3\xbcrk&#39;s Reforms">Atat\xc3\xbcrk\'s Reforms</a>, although unlike the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">Russian Revolution</a> of the same time period, it did not result in the adoption of <a href="/wiki/State_atheism" title="State atheism">state atheism</a>.\n</p><p>The degree to which an official national religion is imposed upon citizens by the state in contemporary society varies considerably; from high as in <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Saudi_Arabia" title="Religion in Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> to minimal or none at all as in <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Denmark" title="Religion in Denmark">Denmark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_England" title="Religion in England">England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Iceland" title="Religion in Iceland">Iceland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Greece" title="Religion in Greece">Greece</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Types">Types</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=State_religion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Types">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The degree and nature of state backing for denomination or creed designated as a state religion can vary. It can range from mere endorsement (with or without financial support) with freedom for other faiths to practice, to prohibiting any competing religious body from operating and to persecuting the followers of other sects. In Europe, competition between <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a> denominations for state sponsorship in the 16th century evolved the principle <i><a href="/wiki/Cuius_regio,_eius_religio" title="Cuius regio, eius religio">Cuius regio, eius religio</a></i> (states follow the religion of the ruler) embodied in the text of the treaty that marked the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Augsburg" title="Peace of Augsburg">Peace of Augsburg</a>, 1555. In <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII_of_England" title="Henry VIII of England">Henry VIII</a> broke with Rome in 1534, being declared the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Head_of_the_Church_of_England" title="Supreme Head of the Church of England">Supreme Head of the Church of England</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> the official religion of England continued to be "Catholicism without the Pope" until after his death in 1547,<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> while in <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Scotland" title="Church of Scotland">Church of Scotland</a> opposed the religion of the ruler.\n</p><p>In some cases, an administrative region may sponsor and fund a set of religious denominations; such is the case in <a href="/wiki/Alsace-Moselle" class="mw-redirect" title="Alsace-Moselle">Alsace-Moselle</a> in <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> under its <a href="/wiki/Local_law_in_Alsace-Moselle" title="Local law in Alsace-Moselle">local law</a>, following the pre-1905 French concordatry legal system and patterns in <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In some <a href="/wiki/Communist_state" title="Communist state">communist states</a>, notably in <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_North_Korea" title="Religion in North Korea">North Korea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Cuba" title="Religion in Cuba">Cuba</a>, the state sponsors religious organizations, and activities outside those state-sponsored religious organizations are met with various degrees of official disapproval. In these cases, state religions are widely seen as efforts by the state to prevent alternate sources of authority.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="State_churches">State churches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=State_religion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: State churches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>There is also a difference between a "state church" and the broader term of "state religion".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> A "state church" is a state religion created by a state for use exclusively by that state.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (March 2016)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> An example of a "state religion" that is not also a "state church" is <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholicism</a> in Costa Rica, which was accepted as the state religion in the 1949 Constitution, despite the lack of a <a href="/wiki/National_church" title="National church">national church</a>. In the case of a "state church", the state has absolute control over the church,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> but in the case of a "state religion", the church is ruled by an exterior body; in the case of Catholicism, the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Vatican</a> has control over the church. In either case, the official state religion has some influence over the ruling of the state.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> As of 2012, there are only five state churches left,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (November 2016)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> as most countries that once featured state churches have <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_church_and_State" class="mw-redirect" title="Separation of church and State">separated the church from their government</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Disestablishment">Disestablishment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=State_religion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Disestablishment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Secular_state" title="Secular state">Secular state</a></div>\n<p>Disestablishment is the process of repealing a church\'s status as an organ of the state. Opponents of disestablishment of the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> were known as <a href="/wiki/Antidisestablishmentarianism" title="Antidisestablishmentarianism">antidisestablishmentarians</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_state_religions">Current state religions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=State_religion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Current state religions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Currently, the following religions have been established as state religions in some countries. All are versions of <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> or <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Buddhism">Buddhism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=State_religion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Buddhism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Governments where <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, either a specific form of, or the whole, has been established as an official religion:\n</p>\n<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Flag_of_Bhutan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Bhutan.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Flag_of_Bhutan.svg/35px-Flag_of_Bhutan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Flag_of_Bhutan.svg/45px-Flag_of_Bhutan.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Bhutan" title="Bhutan">Bhutan</a>: The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Bhutan" title="Constitution of Bhutan">Constitution</a> defines Buddhism as the "spiritual heritage of Bhutan" and mandates that <a href="/wiki/Druk_Gyalpo" title="Druk Gyalpo">Druk Gyalpo</a> (King) should appoint <a href="/wiki/Je_Khenpo" title="Je Khenpo">Je Khenpo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dratshang_Lhentshog" title="Dratshang Lhentshog">Dratshang Lhentshog</a> (The Commission for the Monastic Affairs).<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Flag_of_Cambodia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Cambodia.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Flag_of_Cambodia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Cambodia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Flag_of_Cambodia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Cambodia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="625" data-file-height="400" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a>: The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Cambodia" class="mw-redirect" title="Constitution of Cambodia">Constitution</a> declared Buddhism as official religion of the country. About 97% of the Cambodia\'s population is Buddhist.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Flag_of_Laos.svg/23px-Flag_of_Laos.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Flag_of_Laos.svg/35px-Flag_of_Laos.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Flag_of_Laos.svg/45px-Flag_of_Laos.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="400" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">Laos</a>: According to Laos constitution, Buddhism is given special privilege in the society of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Flag_of_Myanmar.svg/23px-Flag_of_Myanmar.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Flag_of_Myanmar.svg/35px-Flag_of_Myanmar.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Flag_of_Myanmar.svg/45px-Flag_of_Myanmar.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a>: Section 361 of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Myanmar" title="Constitution of Myanmar">Constitution</a> states that "The Union recognizes special position of Buddhism as the faith professed by the great majority of the citizens of the Union."<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Flag_of_Sri_Lanka.svg/23px-Flag_of_Sri_Lanka.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Flag_of_Sri_Lanka.svg/35px-Flag_of_Sri_Lanka.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Flag_of_Sri_Lanka.svg/46px-Flag_of_Sri_Lanka.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Constitution of Sri Lanka">constitution of Sri Lanka</a> accords Buddhism the "foremost place", although it does not identify it as a state religion. Buddhism is given special privileges in Sri Lankan constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_Thailand.svg/23px-Flag_of_Thailand.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_Thailand.svg/35px-Flag_of_Thailand.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_Thailand.svg/45px-Flag_of_Thailand.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>: According to <a href="/wiki/Thai_constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="Thai constitution">Thai constitution</a> the country is secular and <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">freedom of religion</a> is guaranteed but some important privileges are also given to Buddhism such as giving money to Buddhist monks to construct Buddhist temples.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Christianity">Christianity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=State_religion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Christianity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Christian_state" title="Christian state">Christian state</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christianity_and_politics" title="Christianity and politics">Christianity and politics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christian_democracy" title="Christian democracy">Christian democracy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Christendom" title="Christendom">Christendom</a></div>\n<p>The following states recognize some form of <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> as their state or official religion (by denomination):\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=State_religion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Roman Catholicism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Jurisdictions where <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholicism</a> has been established as a state or official religion:\n</p>\n<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Flag_of_Costa_Rica.svg/23px-Flag_of_Costa_Rica.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Flag_of_Costa_Rica.svg/35px-Flag_of_Costa_Rica.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Flag_of_Costa_Rica.svg/46px-Flag_of_Costa_Rica.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">Costa Rica</a>: article 75 of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Costa_Rica" title="Constitution of Costa Rica">constitution of Costa Rica</a> confirms that "The Roman Catholic and Apostolic Religion is the religion of the State, which contributes to its maintenance, without preventing the free exercise in the Republic of other forms of worship that are not opposed to universal morality or good customs."<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Flag_of_Liechtenstein.svg/23px-Flag_of_Liechtenstein.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Flag_of_Liechtenstein.svg/35px-Flag_of_Liechtenstein.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Flag_of_Liechtenstein.svg/46px-Flag_of_Liechtenstein.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Liechtenstein" title="Constitution of Liechtenstein">constitution of Liechtenstein</a> describes the Catholic Church as the state religion and enjoying "the full protection of the State". The constitution does however ensure that people of other faiths \'"shall be entitled to practise their creeds and to hold religious services to the extent consistent with morality and public order."<sup id="cite_ref-LiechtensteinConstitution_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LiechtensteinConstitution-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Flag_of_Malta.svg/23px-Flag_of_Malta.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Flag_of_Malta.svg/35px-Flag_of_Malta.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Flag_of_Malta.svg/45px-Flag_of_Malta.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>: Article 2 of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Malta" title="Constitution of Malta">Constitution of Malta</a> declares that "the religion of Malta is the Roman Catholic Apostolic Religion"<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Flag_of_Monaco.svg/19px-Flag_of_Monaco.svg.png" width="19" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Flag_of_Monaco.svg/29px-Flag_of_Monaco.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Flag_of_Monaco.svg/38px-Flag_of_Monaco.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a>: article 9 of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Monaco" title="Constitution of Monaco">constitution of Monaco</a> describes the catholic, <a href="/wiki/Apostolic_succession" title="Apostolic succession">apostolic</a> and Roman religion as the religion of the state.<sup id="cite_ref-MonacoReligion_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MonacoReligion-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg/16px-Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg.png" width="16" height="16" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg/24px-Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg/32px-Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="500" />&#160;&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City</a>: the Vatican is an <a href="/wiki/Elective_monarchy" title="Elective monarchy">Elective</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theocracy" title="Theocracy">Theocratic</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Sacerdotal_state" title="Sacerdotal state">sacerdotal</a> <a href="/wiki/Absolute_Monarchy" class="mw-redirect" title="Absolute Monarchy">Absolute Monarchy</a><sup id="cite_ref-pages_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pages-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> ruled by the Pope, who is also the <a href="/wiki/Vicar" title="Vicar">Vicar</a> of the Catholic Church. The highest state functionaries are all <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a> clergy of various national origins. It is the sovereign territory of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a> (<a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin</a>: <i lang="la">Sancta Sedes</i>) and the location of the Pope\'s official residence, referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Apostolic_Palace" title="Apostolic Palace">Apostolic Palace</a>.</li></ul>\n<p>Jurisdictions that give various degrees of recognition in their constitutions to Roman Catholicism without establishing it as the state religion:\n</p>\n<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Flag_of_Andorra.svg/22px-Flag_of_Andorra.svg.png" width="22" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Flag_of_Andorra.svg/33px-Flag_of_Andorra.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Flag_of_Andorra.svg/43px-Flag_of_Andorra.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="700" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Flag_of_Argentina.svg/23px-Flag_of_Argentina.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Flag_of_Argentina.svg/35px-Flag_of_Argentina.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Flag_of_Argentina.svg/46px-Flag_of_Argentina.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="500" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> \xe2\x80\x93 article 2 of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Argentina" title="Constitution of Argentina">Constitution</a> explicitly states that the government supports the Roman Catholic Apostolic Faith, but the constitution does not establish a state religion.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Flag_of_the_Dominican_Republic.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Dominican_Republic.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Flag_of_the_Dominican_Republic.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Dominican_Republic.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Flag_of_the_Dominican_Republic.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_Dominican_Republic.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="500" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Flag_of_El_Salvador.svg/23px-Flag_of_El_Salvador.svg.png" width="23" height="13" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Flag_of_El_Salvador.svg/35px-Flag_of_El_Salvador.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Flag_of_El_Salvador.svg/46px-Flag_of_El_Salvador.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1064" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">El Salvador</a></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Flag_of_Haiti.svg/23px-Flag_of_Haiti.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Flag_of_Haiti.svg/35px-Flag_of_Haiti.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Flag_of_Haiti.svg/46px-Flag_of_Haiti.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="300" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a> <sup id="cite_ref-CIAhaiti_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIAhaiti-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Flag_of_Panama.svg/23px-Flag_of_Panama.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Flag_of_Panama.svg/45px-Flag_of_Panama.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="300" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a> \xe2\x80\x93 the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Panama" title="Constitution of Panama">Constitution</a> recognizes Catholicism as "the religion of the majority" of citizens but does not designate it as the official state religion.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" title="Paraguay">Paraguay</a><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/12/Flag_of_Poland.svg/23px-Flag_of_Poland.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/12/Flag_of_Poland.svg/46px-Flag_of_Poland.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="800" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Eastern_Orthodoxy">Eastern Orthodoxy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=State_religion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Eastern Orthodoxy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The jurisdictions below give various degrees of recognition in their constitutions to <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodoxy" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodoxy">Eastern Orthodoxy</a>, but without establishing it as the state religion:\n</p>\n<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg/23px-Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg/35px-Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg/46px-Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>: in the Bulgarian Constitution, the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Orthodox_Church" title="Bulgarian Orthodox Church">Bulgarian Orthodox Church</a> is recognized as "the traditional religion" of the Bulgarian people, but the state itself remains secular.</li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Flag_of_Georgia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Georgia.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Flag_of_Georgia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Georgia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Flag_of_Georgia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Georgia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>: <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Orthodox_Church" title="Georgian Orthodox Church">Georgian Orthodox Church</a> is not the state church of Georgia but has a special constitutional agreement with the state, with the constitution recognising "the special role of the Apostolic Autocephalous Orthodox Church of Georgia in the history of Georgia and its independence from the state."<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> (See also <a href="/wiki/Concordat_of_2002" title="Concordat of 2002">Concordat of 2002</a>)</li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Flag_of_Greece.svg/23px-Flag_of_Greece.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Flag_of_Greece.svg/35px-Flag_of_Greece.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Flag_of_Greece.svg/45px-Flag_of_Greece.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="400" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>: The <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Greece" title="Church of Greece">Church of Greece</a> is recognized by the Greek Constitution as the prevailing religion in Greece.<sup id="cite_ref-GreeceConstitution_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GreeceConstitution-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> However, this provision does not give official status to the Church of Greece, while all other religions are recognized as equal and may be practiced freely.<sup id="cite_ref-GreeceConstitution2_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GreeceConstitution2-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Protestantism">Protestantism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=State_religion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Protestantism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Anglicanism">Anglicanism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=State_religion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Anglicanism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<p>The Anglican <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> is the established church in England as well as all three of the <a href="/wiki/Crown_Dependencies" class="mw-redirect" title="Crown Dependencies">Crown Dependencies</a>.\n</p>\n<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/be/Flag_of_England.svg/23px-Flag_of_England.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/be/Flag_of_England.svg/35px-Flag_of_England.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/be/Flag_of_England.svg/46px-Flag_of_England.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="480" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> is the established church in England, but not in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> as a whole.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> It is the only established Anglican church worldwide. The Anglican <a href="/wiki/Church_in_Wales" title="Church in Wales">Church in Wales</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Episcopal_Church" title="Scottish Episcopal Church">Scottish Episcopal Church</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Ireland" title="Church of Ireland">Church of Ireland</a> are not established churches and they are independent from the Church of England. The <a href="/wiki/British_monarchy" class="mw-redirect" title="British monarchy">British monarch</a> is the titular <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Governor_of_the_Church_of_England" title="Supreme Governor of the Church of England">Supreme Governor of the Church of England</a>. The 26 most senior bishops in the Church of England are <a href="/wiki/Lords_Spiritual" title="Lords Spiritual">Lords Spiritual</a> and have seats in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">House of Lords</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">UK Parliament</a>.</li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_Guernsey.svg/23px-Flag_of_Guernsey.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_Guernsey.svg/35px-Flag_of_Guernsey.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_Guernsey.svg/45px-Flag_of_Guernsey.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Guernsey" title="Guernsey">Guernsey</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> is the established church in the <a href="/wiki/Bailiwick_of_Guernsey" title="Bailiwick of Guernsey">Bailiwick of Guernsey</a>, and the leader of the Church of England in the territory is the <a href="/wiki/Dean_of_Guernsey" title="Dean of Guernsey">Dean of Guernsey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Flag_of_the_Isle_of_Man.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Isle_of_Man.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Flag_of_the_Isle_of_Man.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Isle_of_Man.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Flag_of_the_Isle_of_Man.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_Isle_of_Man.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="300" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> is the established church on the Isle of Man. The <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Sodor_and_Man" title="Bishop of Sodor and Man">Bishop of Sodor and Man</a> is an ex officio member of the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Council_of_the_Isle_of_Man" title="Legislative Council of the Isle of Man">Legislative Council</a> of the upper house of the <a href="/wiki/Tynwald" title="Tynwald">Tynwald</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Flag_of_Jersey.svg/23px-Flag_of_Jersey.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Flag_of_Jersey.svg/35px-Flag_of_Jersey.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Flag_of_Jersey.svg/46px-Flag_of_Jersey.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">Jersey</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> is the established church in <a href="/wiki/Bailiwick_of_Jersey" class="mw-redirect" title="Bailiwick of Jersey">Jersey</a>, and the leader of the church on the island is the <a href="/wiki/Dean_of_Jersey" title="Dean of Jersey">Dean of Jersey</a>, a non-voting member of the <a href="/wiki/States_of_Jersey" title="States of Jersey">States of Jersey</a>.</li></ul>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Calvinism">Calvinism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=State_religion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Calvinism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Flag_of_Tuvalu.svg/23px-Flag_of_Tuvalu.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Flag_of_Tuvalu.svg/35px-Flag_of_Tuvalu.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Flag_of_Tuvalu.svg/46px-Flag_of_Tuvalu.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a>: The <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Tuvalu" title="Church of Tuvalu">Church of Tuvalu</a> is the state religion, although in practice this merely entitles it to "the privilege of performing special services on major national events".<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Tuvalu" title="Constitution of Tuvalu">Constitution of Tuvalu</a> guarantees freedom of religion, including the freedom to practice, the freedom to change religion, the right not to receive religious instruction at school or to attend religious ceremonies at school, and the right not to "take an oath or make an affirmation that is contrary to his religion or belief".<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Lutheranism">Lutheranism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=State_religion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Lutheranism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<p>Jurisdictions where a <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheran</a> church has been established as a state religion include the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_countries" title="Nordic countries">Nordic countries</a> (as of 2012 Norway does not have a public religion<sup id="cite_ref-snl.no_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-snl.no-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>).\n</p>\n<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Flag_of_Denmark.svg/20px-Flag_of_Denmark.svg.png" width="20" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Flag_of_Denmark.svg/31px-Flag_of_Denmark.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Flag_of_Denmark.svg/40px-Flag_of_Denmark.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="740" data-file-height="560" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>: section 4 of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Denmark" title="Constitution of Denmark">Constitution of Denmark</a> confirms the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Denmark" title="Church of Denmark">Church of Denmark</a> as the "established" church.<sup id="cite_ref-DenmarkConstitution_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DenmarkConstitution-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Flag_of_the_Faroe_Islands.svg/21px-Flag_of_the_Faroe_Islands.svg.png" width="21" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Flag_of_the_Faroe_Islands.svg/32px-Flag_of_the_Faroe_Islands.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Flag_of_the_Faroe_Islands.svg/41px-Flag_of_the_Faroe_Islands.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1100" data-file-height="800" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands" title="Faroe Islands">Faroe Islands</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Faroe_Islands" title="Church of the Faroe Islands">Church of the Faroe Islands</a> is the state church of the <a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands" title="Faroe Islands">Faroe Islands</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_administrative_division" title="Autonomous administrative division">autonomous</a> country within the <a href="/wiki/Danish_Realm" class="mw-redirect" title="Danish Realm">Danish Realm</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Flag_of_Greenland.svg/23px-Flag_of_Greenland.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Flag_of_Greenland.svg/35px-Flag_of_Greenland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Flag_of_Greenland.svg/45px-Flag_of_Greenland.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Denmark" title="Church of Denmark">Church of Denmark</a> is the state church of <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_administrative_division" title="Autonomous administrative division">autonomous</a> country within the <a href="/wiki/Danish_Realm" class="mw-redirect" title="Danish Realm">Danish Realm</a>.</li></ul></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Flag_of_Finland.svg/23px-Flag_of_Finland.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Flag_of_Finland.svg/35px-Flag_of_Finland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Flag_of_Finland.svg/46px-Flag_of_Finland.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1100" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Lutheran_Church_of_Finland" title="Evangelical Lutheran Church of Finland">Evangelical Lutheran Church of Finland</a> has a special relationship with the Finnish state, its internal structure being described in a special law, the Church Act.<sup id="cite_ref-FinlandConstitution_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FinlandConstitution-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The Church Act can be amended only by a decision of the synod of the Evangelical Lutheran Church and subsequent ratification by the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Finland" title="Parliament of Finland">Parliament of Finland</a>. The Church Act is protected by the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Finland" title="Constitution of Finland">Constitution of Finland</a> and the state can not change the Church Act without changing the constitution. The church has a power to tax its members. The state collects these taxes for the church, for a fee. On the other hand, the church is required to give a burial place for everyone in its graveyards.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Finland" title="President of Finland">President of Finland</a> also decides the themes for intercession days. The church does not consider itself a state church, as the Finnish state does not have the power to influence its internal workings or its theology, although it has a veto in those changes of the internal structure which require changing the Church Act. Neither does the Finnish state accord any precedence to Lutherans or the Lutheran faith in its own acts. The <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Freethinkers_of_Finland" title="Union of Freethinkers of Finland">Union of Freethinkers of Finland</a> has criticized the official endorsement of the two churches by the Finnish state, and has campaigned for the separation of church and state.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Flag_of_Iceland.svg/21px-Flag_of_Iceland.svg.png" width="21" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Flag_of_Iceland.svg/32px-Flag_of_Iceland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Flag_of_Iceland.svg/42px-Flag_of_Iceland.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="576" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Iceland" title="Constitution of Iceland">Constitution of Iceland</a> confirms the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Iceland" title="Church of Iceland">Church of Iceland</a> as the state church of Iceland.<sup id="cite_ref-IcelandConstitution_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IcelandConstitution-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Flag_of_Norway.svg/21px-Flag_of_Norway.svg.png" width="21" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Flag_of_Norway.svg/32px-Flag_of_Norway.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Flag_of_Norway.svg/41px-Flag_of_Norway.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1100" data-file-height="800" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>: A bill passed in 2016 and effective as of 1 January 2017 created the Church of Norway as an independent legal entity.<sup id="cite_ref-regjeringen.no_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regjeringen.no-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-stortinget.no_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stortinget.no-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Norway" title="Constitution of Norway">Constitution of Norway</a> Article 16 stipulates that "The <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Norway" title="Church of Norway">Church of Norway</a>, an Evangelical-Lutheran church, will remain the Established Church of Norway and will as such be supported by the State".<sup id="cite_ref-:0_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The Norwegian wording in Article 16 "folkekirke" (literally "people\'s church") is officially translated as "established church".  The actual meaning and implications of "folkekirke" remain contested.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> This was amended in 2012, from "Evangelical-Lutheran religion remains the public religion of the State"<sup id="cite_ref-abcnyheter_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abcnyheter-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> and since 2012 Norway does not have a public religion.<sup id="cite_ref-snl.no_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-snl.no-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The Church of Norway will still obtain financial support from the state of Norway, along with other religious communities.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/23px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/35px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/46px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1000" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Sweden" title="Church of Sweden">Church of Sweden</a> was until 2000 the official state church of Sweden, and Lutheranism was therefore the state religion of Sweden. In spite of the separation between the state and the church in 2000, the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Sweden" title="Church of Sweden">Church of Sweden</a> still has a special status in Sweden. Sweden is therefore often seen as a midway between having a state religion and not.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The church has its own legal regulation in the 1998 Church of Sweden Act, which regulates the church\'s basic structure, creeds and right to tax members of the church. According to the Act, the Church of Sweden must be a democratic, Lutheran people\'s church. Only the Swedish <a href="/wiki/Riksdag" title="Riksdag">Riksdag</a> can change this fact. The connections to the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_royal_family" title="Swedish royal family">Swedish royal family</a> are complicated. For example, the Swedish constitution stipulates that the <a href="/wiki/Monarch_of_Sweden" class="mw-redirect" title="Monarch of Sweden">Monarch of Sweden</a> must be a true Lutheran, accepting the doctrine of the Church of Sweden. All members of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_house" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal house">royal house</a> must accept the same doctrine to be able to inherit the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Sweden" title="Monarchy of Sweden">Throne of Sweden</a>. The parishes of the Church of Sweden were the smallest administrative entities in Sweden and were used as civil registration and taxation units until 1 January 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h4><span id="Other.2FMixed"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Other/Mixed">Other/Mixed</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=State_religion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Other/Mixed">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Flag_of_Armenia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Armenia.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Flag_of_Armenia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Armenia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Flag_of_Armenia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Armenia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a>: <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Apostolic_Church" title="Armenian Apostolic Church">Armenian Apostolic Church</a> is not the state church of <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a> but has a special constitutional agreement with the state, with the constitution recognising "The Republic of Armenia shall recognise the exclusive mission of the Armenian Apostolic Holy Church, as a national church, in the spiritual life of the Armenian people, in the development of their national culture and preservation of their national identity."<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/35px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/45px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>: The <a href="/wiki/Local_law_in_Alsace-Moselle" title="Local law in Alsace-Moselle">local law in Alsace-Moselle</a> accords official status to four religions in this specific region of France: <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheranism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Calvinism" title="Calvinism">Calvinism</a>. The law is a remnant of the Napoleonic <a href="/wiki/Concordat_of_1801" title="Concordat of 1801">Concordat of 1801</a>, which was abrogated in the rest of France by the <a href="/wiki/1905_French_law_on_the_separation_of_Church_and_State" class="mw-redirect" title="1905 French law on the separation of Church and State">law of 1905</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_church_and_state" title="Separation of church and state">separation of church and state</a>.  However, at the time, Alsace-Moselle had been <a href="/wiki/Alsace-Lorraine" title="Alsace-Lorraine">annexed by Germany</a>. The Concordat therefore remained in force in these areas, and it was not abrogated when France regained control of the region in 1918. Therefore, the separation of church and state, part of the French concept of <a href="/wiki/La%C3%AFcit%C3%A9" title="La\xc3\xafcit\xc3\xa9">La\xc3\xafcit\xc3\xa9</a>, does not apply in this region.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Flag_of_Hungary.svg/23px-Flag_of_Hungary.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Flag_of_Hungary.svg/35px-Flag_of_Hungary.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Flag_of_Hungary.svg/46px-Flag_of_Hungary.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>: The preamble to the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Hungary" title="Constitution of Hungary">Hungarian Constitution of 2011</a> describes Hungary as "part of Christian Europe" and acknowledges "the role of Christianity in preserving nationhood", while Article VII provides that "the State shall cooperate with the Churches for community goals". However, the constitution also guarantees freedom of religion and separation of church and state.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Flag_of_Lebanon.svg/23px-Flag_of_Lebanon.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Flag_of_Lebanon.svg/35px-Flag_of_Lebanon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Flag_of_Lebanon.svg/45px-Flag_of_Lebanon.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="500" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>: There are 18 officially recognized religious groups in Lebanon, each with its own family law legislation and set of religious courts.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Flag_of_Samoa.svg/23px-Flag_of_Samoa.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Flag_of_Samoa.svg/35px-Flag_of_Samoa.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Flag_of_Samoa.svg/46px-Flag_of_Samoa.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2880" data-file-height="1440" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Samoa" title="Samoa">Samoa</a>: In June 2017, Parliament voted to amend the wording of Article 1 of the constitution, thereby making Christianity the state religion. The status of the religion had previously only been mentioned in the preamble, which prime minister <a href="/wiki/Tuilaepa_Aiono_Sailele_Malielegaoi" title="Tuilaepa Aiono Sailele Malielegaoi">Tuilaepa Aiono Sailele Malielegaoi</a> considered legally inadequate.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Flag_of_Zambia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Zambia.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Flag_of_Zambia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Zambia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Flag_of_Zambia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Zambia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1400" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a>: The preamble to the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Zambia" title="Constitution of Zambia">Zambian Constitution of 1991</a> declares Zambia to be "a Christian nation", while also guaranteeing freedom of religion.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Islam">Islam</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=State_religion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Islam">edit</a><span title="Islamic religious police">Islamic religious police</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Islamism" title="Islamism">Islamism</a></div>\n<p>Many <a href="/wiki/List_of_Muslim-majority_countries" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Muslim-majority countries">Muslim-majority countries</a> have constitutionally established Islam, or a specific form of it, as a state religion. <a href="/wiki/Proselytism" title="Proselytism">Proselytism</a> (converting people to another religion) is often illegal.\n</p>\n<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" Its religion is Islam."<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Flag_of_Somalia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Somalia.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Flag_of_Somalia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Somalia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Flag_of_Somalia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Somalia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>: Article 2 of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Somalia" title="Constitution of Somalia">Provisional Constitution of the Federal Republic of Somalia</a>: "Islam is the religion of the State."<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Flag_of_Tunisia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Tunisia.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Flag_of_Tunisia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Tunisia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Flag_of_Tunisia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Tunisia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a>: Article 1 and 6 of the <a href="/wiki/Tunisian_Constitution_of_2014" title="Tunisian Constitution of 2014">Tunisian Constitution of 2014</a>: "Tunisia is a free, independent, sovereign state; its religion is Islam (...) The state is the guardian of religion. It guarantees freedom of conscience and belief, the free exercise of religious practices and the neutrality of mosques and places of worship from all partisan instrumentalisation."<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder"
